  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b25d0c18-039a-434a-ae5a-be87120ca094'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer14693648263504622561">Bayport High operates like any other high school--jocks at the top, outsiders at the bottom, and everyone else in between.   <span id="freeText14693648263504622561" style="display:none">Bayport High operates like any other high school--jocks at the top, outsiders at the bottom, and everyone else in between. Enter Toby Klein, a sophomore computer hacker who doesn't play well with others. She has zero school spirit, a black belt in karate, and what her guidance counselor calls an attitude problem. She's the last person you'd expect to be invited to join the varsity cheerleading squad.<br />But things are different at Bayport.<br />Bayport's varsity cheer squad is made up of the hottest of the hot. But this A-list is dangerous in more ways than one. The Squad is actually a cover for the most highly trained group of underage government operatives the United States has ever assembled. Athletically, they're unmatchable, though they make it all look easy on the field. Mentally, they're exceptional--but with one flash of their gorgeous smiles, you'll completely forget that. Socially, they're gifted, so they can command and manipulate any situation. And above all, they have the perfect cover, because, beyond herkies and highlights, no one expects anything from a cheerleader.<br />Toby Klein might not seem like the most likely recruit, but she's never been one to turn down a challenge. If she can handle the makeover, Bayport Hight may just have found its newest cheerleader.<br /><br />Pretty, popular, armed, and <i>extremely</i> dangerous--meet <b>THE SQUAD</b>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5401939325509248206"><br/><b>OH MY GOD. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/421313.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've just found out I almost died today.</b><br/><br/><br/>From Wikipedia:<br/><br/><i>Death from laughter refers to a rare instance of death, usually resulting from <u>cardiac arrest or asphyxiation</u>, caused by a fit of laughter. Instances of death by laughter have been recorded from Ancient Greece to the modern day. The first recorded use of the alternative term fatal hilarity is from 1956.<br/>Death may result from several pathologies that deviate from benign laughter. Infarction of the pons and medulla oblongata in the b</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5401939325509248206" style="display:none"><br><b>OH MY GOD. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/421313.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've just found out I almost died today.</b><br><br><br>From Wikipedia:<br><br><i>Death from laughter refers to a rare instance of death, usually resulting from <u>cardiac arrest or asphyxiation</u>, caused by a fit of laughter. Instances of death by laughter have been recorded from Ancient Greece to the modern day. The first recorded use of the alternative term fatal hilarity is from 1956.<br>Death may result from several pathologies that deviate from benign laughter. Infarction of the pons and medulla oblongata in the brain may cause pathological laughter.<br>Laughter can cause <u>atonia and collapse ("gelastic syncope")</u>, which in turn can cause <u>trauma</u>. See also <u>laughter-induced syncope, cataplexy, and Bezold-Jarisch reflex</u>. Gelastic seizures can be due to focal <u>lesions to the hypothalamus</u>. Depending upon the size of the lesion, the emotional lability may be a sign of an acute condition, and not itself the cause of the fatality. Gelastic syncope has also been associated with the cerebellum.</i><br><br><br>See?<br><br><b>This book tried to kill me.</b><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5401939325509248206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_805762870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/805762870" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/805762870?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=adorable-favourites">adorable-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805762870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11469231896388356367"><b>I AM OFFICIALLY IN LOVE WITH JLB! ♥</b><br/><br/>I'm in daze of re-reading a bunch of books I previously enjoyed, and after going through the many JLB books I've already read, I decided to get on this series -- and it. Was. Awesome! <br/><br/>Basically, at Toby's school, the cheerleaders rule with their perky happiness and sociable intuitiveness, being called the "God Squad" for a reason -- which is why Toby is so surprised when she gets an invite to join. In code. Multiple codes, actually which the hacker in her autom</span>
  <span id="freeText11469231896388356367" style="display:none"><b>I AM OFFICIALLY IN LOVE WITH JLB! ♥</b><br /><br />I'm in daze of re-reading a bunch of books I previously enjoyed, and after going through the many JLB books I've already read, I decided to get on this series -- and it. Was. Awesome! <br /><br />Basically, at Toby's school, the cheerleaders rule with their perky happiness and sociable intuitiveness, being called the "God Squad" for a reason -- which is why Toby is so surprised when she gets an invite to join. In code. Multiple codes, actually which the hacker in her automatically figures out with intrigue. <br /><br />And as it turns out? Those perky blonde cheerleaders who seem completely brainless and shallow? They're operatives in a top secret program that trains cheerleaders to undergo undercover missions -- because really, who would suspect the cheerleaders who jump and cheer and sell delicious-yet-awfully-named cookies? <br /><br />Yup. Cheerleader spies. <br /><br />It was laugh-out-loud funny and kiss-my-ass epic! Toby -- our amazing third-degree black-belt computer hacker with sarcasm -- was so cynical and anti-cheerleader that her constant inner horror about all she had to do as a new member of the "God Squad" left me constantly giggling! We're used to reading about girls who want to be popular or at least enjoy it, but this isn't Toby <i>at all</i>. She may be tiny, but she's snarky, she's a computer genius, and she threatens football players on a regular basis for beating up her flirtatious younger brother. <br /><br />I want her to be my new best friend. <br /><br />There's a small budding romance going on between her and Jack, which is super-funny to watch because she's a threat prodigy but a flirt fail -- as in, she kicks more than she bats her eyelashes. Which I guess works because it manages to turn Jack on, but I digress. Jack and Toby, no matter what she tries to argue = ♥<br /><br />JLB always has the most brilliant ideas that are ten million shades of original -- such as <b>Tattoo</b> and <b>The Naturals</b> -- and this is no exception. Her research about everything spy-related was flawless. Her terminology was spot on. I wouldn't be surprised if JLB was a secret spy because she really knows her stuff. <br /><br />My only complaint is that I always wish -- in all her books -- that she goes personal with the characters and the story. Sure, I had fun with all the reactions and interactions and personalities and etcetera, but when her stories constitute as really good, they good be FAN-FLIPPING-TASTIC with a little better execution. <br /><br />Other than that? I will always, always be looking out for anything JLB writes. Always. And you should too :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="11469231896388356367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1397901441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397901441" />
    <a title="Kate " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24113337-kate"><img alt="Kate " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578961161p2/24113337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397901441?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate " href="/user/show/24113337-kate">Kate </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24113337-kate?shelf=do-not-recommend">do-not-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24113337-kate?shelf=spies">spies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397901441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15033737196834387012">Ok, let me start this review of by saying that I actually really love some of JLB’s work - The Fixer and the Naturals series - which is why I decided to read as many of her books as possible. I was really excited for this series because the premise sounds great. I mean cheerleaders as government spies? Sign me up!<br/><br/>Sadly, I was disappointed.<br/>Don't get me wrong, there were a few things that I liked.<br/>Some of the characters (especially Lucy, Zee and Tara) were cool and their base sounded amazing, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText15033737196834387012" style="display:none">Ok, let me start this review of by saying that I actually really love some of JLB’s work - The Fixer and the Naturals series - which is why I decided to read as many of her books as possible. I was really excited for this series because the premise sounds great. I mean cheerleaders as government spies? Sign me up!<br /><br />Sadly, I was disappointed.<br />Don't get me wrong, there were a few things that I liked.<br />Some of the characters (especially Lucy, Zee and Tara) were cool and their base sounded amazing, but that’s sadly about it. <br /><br />There were just a lot of things that irked me about this book. The biggest issue I had was with the main character Toby. She was just so judgmental of the other girls and just felt like she though that she was better than any of the cheerleaders. Mainly because she wasn't one of *those* girls that wear *tons* of make up and have only like 3 braincells since they always smile and cheer etc. No, Toby isn’t that kind of girl. She is *better* because she can be violent, wears combat boots and doesn’t think of the cheerleaders as gods (etc.). Plus she doesn’t have any real experience with boys. She is such a special snowflake. /rant over<br /><br />I have big issues with shaming of any kind and so I really hated that portion of the book. I could have dealt with it if it was executed better. It would have been such a great possibility for character development, but in my opinion that opportunity wasn’t really used. I think that that’s what the author really wanted to do, but it just didn’t ring true in my opinion. It just feels like Toby still mostly looks down on the others and I don't feel like she has changed much.<br /><br />Those are just some of the things that annoyed me. (Also what was up with Toby's brother? And the whole dating thing was just ugh.)<br /><br />All in all, I'd give it a 1.5 to 2 stars. Not really sure at this point. Definitely won't reread this ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15033737196834387012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40763107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40763107" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50448-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175789489p2/50448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40763107?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/50448-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40763107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1524402996659191319"><br/>If you'd told me at the beginning of sophomore year that I was going to end up a government operative, I would have thought you were crazy, but if you'd told me I was destined to become a cheerleader, I would have had you committed, no questions asked. At that point in time, there were three things in life that I knew for certain: 1)I was a girl who'd never met a site she couldn't hack or a code she couldn't break, 2) I had a roundhouse that could put a grown man in the hospital, and 3) I would </span>
  <span id="freeText1524402996659191319" style="display:none"><br />If you'd told me at the beginning of sophomore year that I was going to end up a government operative, I would have thought you were crazy, but if you'd told me I was destined to become a cheerleader, I would have had you committed, no questions asked. At that point in time, there were three things in life that I knew for certain: 1)I was a girl who'd never met a site she couldn't hack or a code she couldn't break, 2) I had a roundhouse that could put a grown man in the hospital, and 3) I would without question chop off my own hands before I'd come within five feet of a pom-pom.<br /><br />I loved this one. I just loved it. We clicked right from the start. The premise? Practically perfect, an unlikely girl, Toby Klein, is invited to try out for the cheerleading squad. Her invitation? It contains a code, and that's not the only suspicious thing going on. Yet before she knows quite how and why it's happening...Toby Klein is...in fact...a cheerleader. True, she's not your typical cheerleader. None of the girls on the squad are...which is why they make perfect undercover agents for the government!<br /><br />I don't want to reveal too much. But I do want you to know that this one is pure fun, and thoroughly satisfying. I know I can't guarantee that YOU will love it as much as I did. Reading is too subjective to make promises like that. But I do encourage you to pick this one up and give it a try. It's a paperback original--and it's worth every penny of the $7.<br /><br /><br />© Becky Laney of Becky's Book Reviews </span>

<div id="review_1439228817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1439228817" />
    <a title="Iris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6341140-iris"><img alt="Iris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323550424p2/6341140.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1439228817?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iris" href="/user/show/6341140-iris">Iris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6341140-iris?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1439228817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9453102730887195969"><b>
  <i>"Tasers and bulletproof push-up bras. In practically the same sentence. So wrong. So, so wrong."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Between this book and The Naturals series, it's safe to say Jennifer Lynn Barnes has a little obsession with teenagers working for CIA/FBI (but The Naturals is waaaay better, just sayin').<br/><br/>Toby Klein is a sophomore student who doesn't fit in with anyone else. She's her own persona and doesn't follow highschool "rules". Until she's invited to join the Cheerleader team... a group of people that Toby </span>
  <span id="freeText9453102730887195969" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Tasers and bulletproof push-up bras. In practically the same sentence. So wrong. So, so wrong."</i>
</b><br /><br />Between this book and The Naturals series, it's safe to say Jennifer Lynn Barnes has a little obsession with teenagers working for CIA/FBI (but The Naturals is waaaay better, just sayin').<br /><br />Toby Klein is a sophomore student who doesn't fit in with anyone else. She's her own persona and doesn't follow highschool "rules". Until she's invited to join the Cheerleader team... a group of people that Toby hates. She then finds out that the Cheerladers are actually undercover CIA agents helping protect the USA from terrorism, bomb attacks and more. It's up to Toby wether or not join the team or live her life as an outsider.<br /><br />I really liked Toby at the beginning. She was witty, funny and didn't take anything way to seriously. She seemed to think for herself and stand up for what she believed. But then, she met The Squad and long gone was the Toby I liked, replaced by a I'll-do-whatever-these-strangers-tell-me Toby. Yeah, not a fan.<br /><br />This book was full of clichés, like Toby liking the type of guy she used to dislike. And then the group of "cheerleaders" was any typical group of girls in any YA book: there a "bitch" one, a "nice" one, a "quiet" one, a "pretty" one, etc. Whatever happened to originality?! There's also a "profiler" (kuddos to Cassie and Dean, I'm guessing?).<br /><br />I gave this book 2 stars because I felt a bit old for this type of story. If I were fifteen-years-old, I'd have loved this book. <br /><br />Not the best Jennifer Lynn Barnes book, but not the worst. The Naturals is so good, tho. And makes more sense. (Cheerleaders working for the CIA, REALLY?!).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9453102730887195969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13716813069507496420">I was really disappointed with this book. I practically had to force myself to finish reading, just because I hate leaving books unfinished. <br/><br/>The biggest problem I had with this book was the main character Toby. <br/>She was constantly complaining throughout the novel; like yes, we get it you're sooooo special because you aren't a cheerleader and you're constantly acting salty about anything and everything girly. The premise of the novel and the idea was good, and I thought the idea of having a spy se</span>
  <span id="freeText13716813069507496420" style="display:none">I was really disappointed with this book. I practically had to force myself to finish reading, just because I hate leaving books unfinished. <br /><br />The biggest problem I had with this book was the main character Toby. <br />She was constantly complaining throughout the novel; like yes, we get it you're sooooo special because you aren't a cheerleader and you're constantly acting salty about anything and everything girly. The premise of the novel and the idea was good, and I thought the idea of having a spy service within a high school would be fun, and make a quick, lighthearted read, however Toby absolutely ruined it. Every paragraph, Toby was complaining about some aspect of being a cheerleader or becoming one of 'those girls'. She thought she was just so much better than everyone else because she didn't wear makeup, and didn't like pop music. I was hoping she'd be a lot more of a badass computer hacker than she actually was- she came off as bratty, self righteous and judgmental. <br /><br />Some of the other characters were cool (I liked Lucy and Tara), but I didn't really love any of them (and Toby's brother was lowkey creepy). None of them really developed throughout the book, especially Toby who was just as judgmental at the end as she was at the start. <br /><br />From the start, I knew I didn't like Toby as a character, but hoped that the plot itself would make up for her lack of interesting qualities. Suffice to say, I was wrong. The plot wasn't exciting at all, and there wasn't really any key moment which had me on the edge of my seat. I thought there was something that the novel would build up to, a big event that would have some lasting impact, but it just kind of happened and there wasn't any real building of suspense. <br /><br />I will not be reading the sequel to this, as I don't want to have to suffer through another book full of Toby's complaining. I guess if you can stand to read that sort of character, and want something easy and not at all meaningful to read then this book is for you. If you like an engaging plot, interesting characters and a buildup of suspense, then I would steer clear. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13716813069507496420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11111546530496284125" style="display:none">I really tried with this one. I kept thinking, if I just got through a few more cliches, stereotypes, horrendous world building, repetitive snark, and self-righteous brats, a kick ass plot would make up for it. <b>I was wrong.</b><br /><br />And Toby, I kept hoping for the badass computer geek I was promised, but all I got was this bratty brat face who thought she was the shit because...<br />a) she didn't know her bra size<br />b) she was almost ubiquitously disliked<br />c) she's never worn makeup<br />d) she finds happiness and being nice overrated<br />e) she beats up anyone who even breathes wrong<br />f) she ACCIDENTALLY hacked the Pentagon (and they just let her be without even worrying about her being a potential terrorist... yeah fucking right)<br />g) she hated everything about her gender except for the spy cover it provided<br /><br />Despite all her crazy self-righteousness, I thought the mystical character growth fairy would poof her into a better person, but <b>I was wrong.</b><br /><br />And, I was under the impression thar book climaxes in an action book were supposed to be exciting and suspenseful, but <b>I was wrong.</b><br /><br />And then I was excited for the feminism that I would find in the idea of cheerleader spies, but, you guessed it <b>I was wrong.</b> Instead of feminism, all I got was the message that caring about your appearance makes you a brat and that the perfect girl was someone who looked like perfection, but didn't want to look nice and complained about looking like a girl every second of the fucking day. <br /><br />So, thank you, <i>Perfect Cover</i> for proving any and all hopes I had for you <b>COMPLETELY WRONG.</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8331390082897629177">I love all things girly, so the idea of cheerleaders who are actually undercover agents? Sign me up. <br/>I could definitely tell that this book was released about 10 years ago, the technological references were <i>very</i> dated, but cool nonetheless.   <span id="freeText8331390082897629177" style="display:none">I love all things girly, so the idea of cheerleaders who are actually undercover agents? Sign me up. <br />I could definitely tell that this book was released about 10 years ago, the technological references were <i>very</i> dated, but cool nonetheless. This book brought me back to middle/high school days when I would’ve absolutely loved this book, back when it was originally released.<br />That being said, this wasn’t my favorite Jennifer Lynn Barnes book, which is so heartbreaking for me to write. I thought that the gadgets (as obsolete as they’d be now) were cool and imaginative. My problem lies within the storyline... to me it was just “meh.” I found that everything that has been planned as part of the operation had happened according to plan. Which, for me isn’t fun to read. I want excitement, twists, scandal. I want to be blown away by all things drama and espionage. I wanted to love this book <i>so</i> much... but it fell short and the ending left me dying for a twist or something dramatic to happen. I wanted shots to be fired or a bomb to go off... anything but how it actually ended. With everyone happy and a small teaser for more “excitement” in the next book. If anything, all it did was turn me off from reading the sequel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1336553796198355590">I did not know what to expect from this series but I have read the 1st 2 books of Jennifer Lynn Barnes "Raised by Wolves" series and really loved them.<br/><br/>This series is about cheerleaders who are also government operatives. This peeked my interest. I am not a girly girl and hated the cheerleaders of my high school but that helped me relate to the main character Toby in this series.<br/><br/>Toby is quick witted, stubborn, tough, and all around tom boy. Toby's plan in life to this point (Sophomore year) was t</span>
  <span id="freeText1336553796198355590" style="display:none">I did not know what to expect from this series but I have read the 1st 2 books of Jennifer Lynn Barnes "Raised by Wolves" series and really loved them.<br /><br />This series is about cheerleaders who are also government operatives. This peeked my interest. I am not a girly girl and hated the cheerleaders of my high school but that helped me relate to the main character Toby in this series.<br /><br />Toby is quick witted, stubborn, tough, and all around tom boy. Toby's plan in life to this point (Sophomore year) was to stay under the radar and perfect her little brother Noah from getting beat up. Instead of flying under the radar she is tapped for the cheerleader squad. Intrigued to know what the hell the note to come to cheerleader tryouts is all about Toby goes.<br /><br />Toby is excepted on the squad due to her expert hacking abilities and is told that the cheerleaders are undercover government agents. Toby can not believe this information until her first test and mission take place. She finds herself with a rush from HACKING into the secured systems and protective of her squad mates (even though she does not like them).<br /><br />Toby's loyalty to the squad and herself are tested. She is doomed to wear sparkles and heels but fights to keep her freedom of "combat boots" attire and attitude.<br /><br />Toby's first mission includes Jack whom she does not like but finds herself thinking about more and more throughout the date/mission. Will she fall for Jack and how will the other 2 cheerleaders who dated Jack before react to her feelings for him if she does?<br /><br />I am onto the 2nd book of this series "The Squad: Killer Spirit"<br /><br />Happy reading.</span>

<div id="review_628727199" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/628727199" />
    <a title="Tiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3171181-tiana"><img alt="Tiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563290056p2/3171181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiana" href="/user/show/3171181-tiana">Tiana</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer628727199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer768530521236336660">I was surprised by how hilarious I thought this book was. Very witty and sarcastic, but usually not overtly so. I'm not sure how that will translate into the second book (if I'll get tired of the voice), but it worked well here. <br/><br/>Toby's attitude and voice literally made me laugh out loud more than once. It's not as "young" as some other spy novels like the Gallagher Girls series (more references to bullet-proof bras, butt photocopying, some swearing, etc.) so I probably won't be giving it to my n</span>
  <span id="freeText768530521236336660" style="display:none">I was surprised by how hilarious I thought this book was. Very witty and sarcastic, but usually not overtly so. I'm not sure how that will translate into the second book (if I'll get tired of the voice), but it worked well here. <br /><br />Toby's attitude and voice literally made me laugh out loud more than once. It's not as "young" as some other spy novels like the Gallagher Girls series (more references to bullet-proof bras, butt photocopying, some swearing, etc.) so I probably won't be giving it to my niece for a few years yet, but it's pretty tame in most respects, at least compared to a lot of the YA books on the market.</span>
  <a data-text-id="768530521236336660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Loved the idea, and enjoyed the action and the snark. Probably because I didn't have to go to school with any cheerleaders.   <span id="freeText17260759068653984211" style="display:none">I'm going to admit right up front--the reason that I read this was because it had a geek/nerd as the MC--one that had to turn herself into a cheerleader so that she could become a spy. Loved the idea, and enjoyed the action and the snark. Probably because I didn't have to go to school with any cheerleaders. The wonders of attending embassy schools and then an American High School where we went split shift (6 am to noon for the first shift, 12:30 to 6:30 for the afternoon shift) and all the jocks and cheerleaders went morning and I went afternoon. (And the morning kids parents got bent out of shape that none of the pm kids EVER attended a sporting event or a pep rally that wasn't held during school hours, thus required. But, as the unofficial class president of the pm kids pointed out--why the he** should we, when we had no idea who any of the jer--er J*O*C*K*S were.) I did enjoy this, and it's here in my house in dead tree format--somewhere. . . (I own about 3500 books in dead tree format plus another 10k or so in electronic. What can I say--I'm a bookaholic and proud of it.) One of those books that is fun to read when the weather is depressing and you don't feel like doing anything.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15492288258815099294"><b>Actual Rating:</b> 3.5 stars<br/><br/><b>Full Review:</b><br/><br/>I definitely had a lot of mixed emotions while reading this book. During the first few chapters, I honestly didn't like it very much at all. I wasn't really connecting with any of the characters (except the main, kind of) and the language is a <i>lot</i>.   <span id="freeText15492288258815099294" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating:</b> 3.5 stars<br /><br /><b>Full Review:</b><br /><br />I definitely had a lot of mixed emotions while reading this book. During the first few chapters, I honestly didn't like it very much at all. I wasn't really connecting with any of the characters (except the main, kind of) and the language is a <i>lot</i>. However, as I got further in, I finally started liking most of the girls. Toby actually reminded me a lot of Macy from Ally Carter's Gallagher Girls series and she made me laugh out loud so many times! <br /><br />All-in-all, I'm definitely going to be picking up the next book, but unfortunately, the high expectations I had for this book were not met. </span>

<div id="review_1436238360" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436238360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2570770279814702620">OMG! I haven't laughed this much in a while!<br/><br/>Here's the cover blurb:<br/><br/>Bayport High operates like any other high school--jocks at the top, outsiders at the bottom, and everyone else in between. Enter Toby Klein, a sophomore computer hacker who doesn't play well with others. She has zero school spirit, a black belt in karate, and what her guidance counselor calls an attitude problem. She's the last person you'd expect to be invited to join the varsity cheerleading squad.<br/>But things are different at Ba</span>
  <span id="freeText2570770279814702620" style="display:none">OMG! I haven't laughed this much in a while!<br /><br />Here's the cover blurb:<br /><br />Bayport High operates like any other high school--jocks at the top, outsiders at the bottom, and everyone else in between. Enter Toby Klein, a sophomore computer hacker who doesn't play well with others. She has zero school spirit, a black belt in karate, and what her guidance counselor calls an attitude problem. She's the last person you'd expect to be invited to join the varsity cheerleading squad.<br />But things are different at Bayport.<br /><br />Bayport's varsity cheer squad is made up of the hottest of the hot. But this A-list is dangerous in more ways than one. The Squad is actually a cover for the most highly trained group of underage government operatives the United States has ever assembled. Athletically, they're unmatchable, though they make it all look easy on the field. Mentally, they're exceptional--but with one flash of their gorgeous smiles, you'll completely forget that. Socially, they're gifted, so they can command and manipulate any situation. And above all, they have the perfect cover, because, beyond herkies and highlights, no one expects anything from a cheerleader.<br />Toby Klein might not seem like the most likely recruit, but she's never been one to turn down a challenge. If she can handle the makeover, Bayport Hight may just have found its newest cheerleader.<br /><br />Pretty, popular, armed, and extremely dangerous--meet THE SQUAD.<br />********<br /><br />Despite being blackmailed onto the "God Squad", Toby manages to hang onto her snarky attitude. When the rest of the student body "discovers" her, the rumors start to fly.<br />**********<br /><br />...."What's her name, anyway?"<br /><br /> "Toby Klein"<br /><br /> And that's when I realized they were talking about me. Silence fell over the classroom, and in one coordinated motion, everyone and their dog leaned toward me, Toby Klein, newly appointed member of the God Squad. They awaited my words with bated breath.<br /><br /> I narrowed my eyes at the whole lot of them, but they just stared curiously back at me. "Boo," I said, trying to dispel their interest.<br /><br /> One of the girls tossed her hair over her shoulder. "That's European for hot," she said loudly, and the entire class looked at me with newfound respect. For the first time in my life, I found myself wishing that a teacher would regain control of her class, but everyone was just way too far gone.<br /><br /> "Toby, you look totally boo today."<br /><br /> Mortified, I glanced back down at my pink sparkly shirt and renewed my vow to terminate the twin fashionazis.<br /><br /> "Talk about boo, where did you get those shoes?"<br /><br /> And now my oversized, clunky, unfashionable boots, the one article of clothing that I'd managed to retain, were being called boo. It was beyond all tolerance. "I am in hell."<br /><br /> The girl who'd asked me about my boots tilted her head to the side. "Is that in the mall?"........... <br /><br />********************<br /><br />....By lunchtime, I'd given up on the idea of homicide. I'd moved on to genocide. I would personally rid the school - nay, the world - of cheerleaders.<br /><br /> "Toby, sit with us."<br /><br /> "Look, there she is!"<br /><br /> "Her? They picked her?"<br /><br /> "Toby Klein? Who's Toby Klein?"<br /><br /> "I hear she's related to Calvin."<br /><br /> "Well, I heard that at her last school, she was like megapopular, but then her boyfriend died, and she swore off popularity forever, but the God Squad, they know these things, and ..."<br /><br /> It was almost more than I could take. How anyone could think I was related to Calvin Klein was completely beyond me.......<br /><br />....Then again, it was hard to believe that I was one "Go Lions" away from being the school's most boo combat-boot-wearing, European, Hollywood offspring of Calvin Klein. I rolled with the punches. ....<br /><br />***************************<br /><br />*snort* Like I said, I laughed my ass off all the way through!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1669722264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1669722264" />
    <a title="LB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18156604-lb"><img alt="LB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370519085p2/18156604.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1669722264?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LB" href="/user/show/18156604-lb">LB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18156604-lb?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18156604-lb?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18156604-lb?shelf=sydney-bristow">sydney-bristow</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1669722264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16239948060958680593">This review is also posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot.com/2016/07/perfect-cover.html'>http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot....</a><br/><br/><br/>Late June/early July has been a rather slow period for me with books, so I decided to dive into another one of Barnes's series since I just inhaled the new Fixer novel and am eagerly awaiting the next installment in The Naturals series.<br/><br/>Perfect Cover, the first novel in The Squad series, isn't quite up to par with Barnes's more recent novels. The plot was kind of bland. Toby gets a few mysterious and coded messages left for her</span>
  <span id="freeText16239948060958680593" style="display:none">This review is also posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot.com/2016/07/perfect-cover.html">http://readingnookandcranny.blogspot....</a><br /><br /><br />Late June/early July has been a rather slow period for me with books, so I decided to dive into another one of Barnes's series since I just inhaled the new Fixer novel and am eagerly awaiting the next installment in The Naturals series.<br /><br />Perfect Cover, the first novel in The Squad series, isn't quite up to par with Barnes's more recent novels. The plot was kind of bland. Toby gets a few mysterious and coded messages left for her, telling her to go meet the Bayport cheer squad members to audition. Since School Spirit is about the last thing on Toby's mind, she isn't all that excited, but goes anyway since they are inviting her with messages written in invisible ink. She shows up, isn't all the impressed, then gets another message, and almost at the snap of the cheer squad's leader's fingers, ends up being a government spy whose cover is a high school cheerleader.<br /><br />Granted, most teenage spy plots have similar eye rolling developments, but everything at the beginning of Perfect Cover happens so quickly I can't help but poke fun at it a little. In fact, I wish Barnes had as well. I think Perfect Cover may suffer from taking itself a little too seriously. It could have used more humor to fluff the plot a little, since the plot is more technology plotting than adventure. Humor could have helped make up for a lack of excitement.<br /><br />Still, Toby is likable enough, and her brother adds a little comic relief. While not a book I would stay up under the covers all night reading obsessively, it's probably a nice light summer read perfect for a day at the beach or a long ride on a plane.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16239948060958680593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_65966768" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65966768" />
    <a title="Reggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2552525-reggie"><img alt="Reggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378516316p2/2552525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65966768?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reggie" href="/user/show/2552525-reggie">Reggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65966768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4968774256062124774">This book was a TEN on the twists and turns scale. The ending was so unexpected. I thought I knew what was going to happen but I was wrong.<br/><br/>I couldn't help but notice it's kind of similar to The Specialists Series. In both books, each person on the team has a special skill. And it's kind of ironic how both series are in the perspective of a computer whiz.<br/><br/>I loved the characterization of Toby. She's sassy, sarcastic, and smart. But the zero to hero thing is a little unrealistic. In reality, someone</span>
  <span id="freeText4968774256062124774" style="display:none">This book was a TEN on the twists and turns scale. The ending was so unexpected. I thought I knew what was going to happen but I was wrong.<br /><br />I couldn't help but notice it's kind of similar to The Specialists Series. In both books, each person on the team has a special skill. And it's kind of ironic how both series are in the perspective of a computer whiz.<br /><br />I loved the characterization of Toby. She's sassy, sarcastic, and smart. But the zero to hero thing is a little unrealistic. In reality, someone like Toby can't be an insignificant nobody (no offense) one day and become an ultra-popular cheerleader the next day. It was a little cliché.<br /><br />I was expecting more action in this book but it didn't have as much. It got a little boring in the middle. It wasn't as fast-paced as I wanted it to be, but oh well. The action that it did have, though, was flawless (the way it was planned). Everything made sense and everything was creative and original.<br /><br />Barnes focused more on explaining (in Toby's POV) each and every team member's special skill and past. I enjoyed getting to know the other teammates and their sometimes not-so-great pasts.<br /><br />The Bottom Line: The unexpected twists and a little hint of romance was enough to keep me wanting more. B :-)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4968774256062124774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66983337" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2557393-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268662323p2/2557393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66983337?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2557393-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2557393-emily?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2557393-emily?shelf=fun-fluff">fun-fluff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66983337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14103299889520281299">High school sophomore Toby Klein is not exactly cheerleader material. She wears combat boots, is a third degree black belt, and spends her spare time hacking into very secure computer systems. So when “the God squad,” as they are frequently referred to, sends her coded notes inviting her to try out, Toby is bewildered and curious, but has no intention of wearing a short skirt and sporting pom-poms. Then she learns that The Squad is a top-secret government program that trains and uses the girls a</span>
  <span id="freeText14103299889520281299" style="display:none">High school sophomore Toby Klein is not exactly cheerleader material. She wears combat boots, is a third degree black belt, and spends her spare time hacking into very secure computer systems. So when “the God squad,” as they are frequently referred to, sends her coded notes inviting her to try out, Toby is bewildered and curious, but has no intention of wearing a short skirt and sporting pom-poms. Then she learns that The Squad is a top-secret government program that trains and uses the girls as spies and when they graduate, they have full CIA credentials. A character describes the program as “Charlie’s Angels meets James Bond meets Bring it On.” The Squad, while unbelievable, is brilliant: who would suspect anything from a cheerleader? The first of a series (there are 2 out now), this book is fun, funny, and fast-paced. The characters are interesting, there are some fun accessories (the bullet-proof push-up bra was my favorite), and it leaves you wanting more. Great for fans of Allie Carter’s Gallagher Girls series (I’d Tell You I Love You, But Then I’d Have to Kill You and Cross My Heart and Hope to Spy) or anyone who likes to throw stereotypes out the window.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14103299889520281299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0jUEpDzn6we6HTONXt034q/Ykg2UTOi7Zo47KVPXNJvSP6Z0f9xG4SJiHKOab5Jp/XmmwZBlv7GVZLbeSE1/EA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15570013885192197588">Jennifer Lynn Barnes (who mostly goes by Jen) was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She has been, in turn, a competitive cheerleader, a volleyball player, a dancer, a debutante, a primate cognition researcher, a teen model, a comic book geek, and a lemur aficionado. She's been writing for as long as she can remember, finished her first full book (which she now refers to as a "practice book" and which none </span>
  <span id="freeText15570013885192197588" style="display:none">Jennifer Lynn Barnes (who mostly goes by Jen) was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She has been, in turn, a competitive cheerleader, a volleyball player, a dancer, a debutante, a primate cognition researcher, a teen model, a comic book geek, and a lemur aficionado. She's been writing for as long as she can remember, finished her first full book (which she now refers to as a "practice book" and which none of you will ever see) when she was still in high school, and then wrote Golden the summer after her freshman year in college, when she was nineteen. <br /><br />Jen graduated high school in 2002, and from Yale University with a degree in cognitive science (the study of the brain and thought) in May of 2006. She'll be spending the 2006-2007 school year abroad, doing autism research at the University of Cambridge in the United Kingdom.</span>
